2014-11-27 22:53:12	@Espyo	and that's when the mipmapping is created

2014-11-27 23:35:10	@Espyo	oh no
2014-11-27 23:35:10	@PikFan	what
2014-11-27 23:35:13	@PikFan	why
2014-11-27 23:35:20	@Espyo	it's a series of really complex events
2014-11-27 23:35:24	@Espyo	but basically...
2014-11-27 23:35:34	@Espyo	instead of drawing the areas one polygon at a time, each time
2014-11-27 23:35:42	@Espyo	I just draw them on an image
2014-11-27 23:35:44	@Espyo	and draw the image instead
2014-11-27 23:35:56	@Espyo	it's a sneaky and less expensive way to do it
2014-11-27 23:36:20	@Espyo	anyway, an option allows you to maximize performance by automatically creating tinier versions of the image
2014-11-27 23:36:37	@Espyo	so that when the engine has to draw the image, but smaller (like when you zoom out), it picks the smaller variant to work with instead
2014-11-27 23:36:45	@Espyo	instead of working on the gigantic 1:1 scale one
2014-11-27 23:37:03	@Espyo	the thing is, the image itself was fine, but because of the way I was creating it, the smaller variants automatically created were all black
2014-11-27 23:37:11	@Espyo	so when the engine was drawing the smaller variants (again, zoom out)...
2014-11-27 23:37:14	@Espyo	it just drew blackness
2014-11-27 23:37:35	@PikFan	strange
2014-11-27 23:37:36	@Espyo	and it happened on Linux because, normally, the images I made aren't liable to use that "smaller variants" technique
2014-11-27 23:37:56	@Espyo	but on Linux, to help with some compatibilities, the framework used there changed the images a bit...
2014-11-27 23:38:05	@Espyo	and in the process made them incidentally liable to use the technique
2014-11-27 23:38:26	@Espyo	so it's a specific operative system doing a broken task on stuff that's working fine
2014-11-27 23:38:31	@Espyo	I had fun figuring this one out, though
2014-11-27 23:42:04	@PikFan	hm, interesting
